# Permissions | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/permissions#permissions)

Permissions

In order to interact with various devices on the terminal, your application needs to declare the relevant permissions for each device. Below is the list of permissions along with their descriptions:

Permission

Description

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_PRINTER

Access the printer

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_MSR

Access the mega stripe reader (MSR)

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_CONTACTLESS\_CARD

Access the contactless card reader (RF card reader)

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_SMARTCARD

Access the smart card reader

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_SERIAL

Access the serial port (RS232)

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_LED

Access the LED device

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_CUSTOMER\_DISPLAY

Access the second display device

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_CLONESCREEN

Access the HDMI device

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_MONEYBOX

Access the cash drawer

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_FINGERPRINT

Access the fingerprint device

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_PIN\_GET\_PIN\_BLOCK

Retrieve the encrypted PIN block by PINPad

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_PIN\_MAC

Calculate the MAC by the MAC key in PINPad

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_PIN\_ENCRYPT\_DATA

Encrypt data by the data key in PINPad

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_PIN\_UPDATE\_USER\_KEY

Update the session (user) key of MasterKey/SessionKey schema

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_SIGNATURE

Access the signature board

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_SAFE\_MODULE

Access HSM

android.permission.SYSTEM\_ALERT\_WINDOW

Used when printing HTML

android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_EXT\_USB\_CTRL

Access the double USB control

Ensure that your application requests and is granted these permissions appropriately to enable seamless interaction with the CloudPOS SDK. For more detailed information, refer to the documentation sections related to each device API and consult the POS Spec, FAQs, or device-specific manuals.

Explore the CloudPOS SDK resources using the quick links provided, including Device API, Device Samples, EMV Development, BarCode Scan, Printer Manual, and TMS Manual.

Thank you for using wizarPOS, and if you have any questions, feel free to explore the available resources or contact our support team.

[PreviousJava API Sampleschevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/java-api-samples)
[NextError codechevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/error-code)

Last updated 1 year ago

# Scanning Service Usage | CloudPOS SDK

This documentation is crafted to aid Android application developers for the Smart POS. It clarifies the functionality of the scanning service and provides details on the released SDKs, testing applications, and features for quickly launching the scan application. For specific downloads and further information, refer to the provided links and sections.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/scanning-service-usage#overview)

Overview

The scanning service enables Android devices equipped with imaging hardware, such as cameras, to scan barcodes or QR codes, retrieving encoded data. This encoded information typically includes a web address, geographic coordinates, small text excerpts, and commercial product codes.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/scanning-service-usage#document)

Document

Version

Download

Release Time

[6arrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/barcodescan/CloudposScannerUsage_3.9.6_en.pdf)

2024-04-11

Scan Barcode Testing Application

[Testing APK Downloadarrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/barcodescan/app-cloudposscannerdemo-20231106.apk)

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/scanning-service-usage#quickly-launch-the-scan-application-in-q2-q3)

Quickly Launch the Scan Application in Q2/Q3

Physical Action: Double-click the power button or long press Volumn+.

This feature enables the swift launch of the scan application. Upon clicking, the system searches for all installed applications and launches the one with the scan intent-filter. If multiple applications exist, the system presents a list for users to choose from, initiating the selected application. The code for the scan intent-filter is as follows:

If no application in the system defines the scan intent-filter, pressing will not work. For instance, to use the scan button effectively, the application must define the scan intent-filter in its Android manifest file, with the category and action defined as follows:

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/scanning-service-usage#cloudpos-scan-service-in-q1-android-4.4)

CloudPOS Scan Service in Q1 Android 4.4

[CloudposScannerService-v3.12.28arrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/CloudposScannerService-v3.12.28-r35144-q1_releasekey_forQ1android4.4.apk)

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/scanning-service-usage#faq)

FAQ

*   How to not show the scan window?
    

Set window\_width=0 and window\_height=0 in ScanParameter.

Generally, physical scanner don't need show the scanner window.

Copy

    <action android:name="android.intent.action.SCAN" />
    <category android:name="android.intent.category.DEFAULT" />

Copy

    <activity
      android:name="com.XX.activity.MainActivity"
      android:label="@string/app_name" >
       <intent-filter>      
         <action android:name="android.intent.action.SCAN" />
         <category android:name="android.intent.category.DEFAULT" />
       </intent-filter>
    </activity>

Device Java API

The Device Java API simplifies development by being packaged as an AAR library file, providing Android developers with easy integration. This API includes functionalities such as Printer, PINPad, MSR, SmartCard, RFCard, SerialPort, LED, Fingerprint, and HSM.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/cloudpos-sdk-aar#versioning)

Versioning

The CloudPOS SDK AAR version number follows the format: Major.Minor.Stage.Build. The main version is updated for architectural changes, the minor version annually, the stage version monthly, and the build version for feature additions or bug fixes.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/cloudpos-sdk-aar#change-history)

Change History

**1.7.7.18**

*   **Add API for switching between external and internal SIM antennas.**
    
*   **Update EMV-related so files.**
    
*   **Add interfaces for MSR swipe, SmartCard attach, RFCard attach, and the last usage time of Printer write.**
    

**1.7.7.13**

*   **Removed the libraries related to sdk\_secondarydisplaylib .**
    
*   **Modified the CustomerDisplayDevice and the corresponding JavaDoc description. The original interface would scale the image to 320\*240 size, but now the size restriction has been removed and images of any size can be passed.**
    
*   **Changed the AbstracAdvancetDevice method to protected.**
    
*   **Fix the error that does not allow the AES algorithm.**
    
*   **Add an API to stop the application.**
    
*   **Adapt HSM to RSA4096 keys.**
    
*   **Provide an interface for the customer display device to obtain the size.**
    
*   **Add an application interface to obtain the last access time of the terminal card - getDeviceLastAccessTime. The terminal's TMSAgent version should be greater than or equal to 5.4.41.**
    
*   **Add paper status detection to the print HTML interface. If an out of paper is detected during printing, return PRINT\_ERROR.**
    

**1.7.7.7**

*   **Fix the bug of isDeviceExist-customerdisplay .**
    
*   **Delete the unimplemented setAccessibilityService and getAccessibilityService methods in the ISystemDevice interface.**
    
*   **Add the method for setting a static IP for Wi-Fi.**
    
*   **Add skipRATS(), calling it before card search can avoid entering 14443-4.**
    
*   **Fix bug of waitForCardAbsent.**
    
*   **Add support for PSAM card slots 5 and 6.**
    
*   **Add Admin/user login/logout interfaces.**
    
*   **Optimize the judgment of whether MSR exists.**

# MDB Communication Protocal | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#introduction)

Introduction

This manual describes the serial communication protocol between Q3 Pos and MDB Interface Board, which will be short as “MIB” in follow content.

The basic baud rate of serial port is set as 115200

As the Q3 POS could be receive command from MIB as a slave, and also could send command to MIB as a master (e.g., send “begin session” command to inform the MDB VMC it’s ready for pay), a mode byte was added in serial frame to show if a command is slave response or a master request.

The request command always anticipates a response command except the checksum is wrong, or the incorrect serial format, in another word, the slave will use silence as a NAK. **Please refer to the** [**documentation** arrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/MDB_interface_board_serial_protocol_20241226.pdf)
**for specific commands and details.**

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#serial-protocol-packet-definition)

Serial Protocol Packet Definition

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#serial-port-parameters)

Serial Port Parameters

*   Baud rate: 115200
    
*   Data format: 8 bits, 1 stop bit, no parity
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#packet-format)

Packet Format

*   Start code: size 1 byte, always be 0x09
    
*   Length: size 1 byte, the number bytes of mode, data, and checksum.
    
*   Mode: size 1 byte, 0x00 means a request packet, 0x01 means a response packet, other value is prohibited.
    
*   Data: size n bytes, The data could be raw MDB commands, such as SETUP, VEND. Or the MIB control commands, such as GET VERSION, SET PARAMETER.
    
*   Checksum: size 1 byte, using LRC algorithm, input data were "mode, data"
    
*   End code: size 1 byte, always be 0x0D.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#specifics)

Specifics

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#mdb-forwarding-mechanism)

MDB Forwarding Mechanism

When the MIB receive the VMC request, it removes the MDB mode bit, fill into serial packet data area, and transmit to serial port. In the opposite direction, the MIB receive the response, it unwraps the packet, and adding mode bit to the tail bytes, sending to the VMC, wait for the acknowledge.MIB will forward all the MDB cashless device commands (MDB spec section 7), except VMC request Poll.

Example: RESET

1.  _VMC -> MIB:_ 0x110 0x10
    
2.  _MIB -> Q3V:_ 0x09 0x04 0x00 0x10 0x10 0xE0 0x0D
    
3.  Q3V _-> MIB:_ 0x09 0x04 0x01 0x00 0x00 0xFF 0x0D
    
4.  _MIB -> VMC:_ 0x00 0x100
    
5.  _VMC -> MIB : 0x00_
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#application-notes)

Application Notes

*   Focus on steps 2 and 3 in the MDB Forwarding Mechanism.
    
*   The application handles all cashless commands except POLL.
    
*   The cashless reader initiates a begin session command to notify the VMC when ready for a transaction.
    
*   MDB raw data includes its checksum byte, distinct from the serial frame checksum.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#a-typical-mdb-transaction-flow)

A Typical MDB Transaction Flow

![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%2Fblobs%2F1fZFmaKVoimHuCqczG14%2FMdb_flow_chart.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=451a1480&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#protocol-command-definition)

Protocol Command Definition

circle-info

Please refer to the [documentation arrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/MDB_interface_board_serial_protocol_20241226.pdf)
for specific commands and details.

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#common-mdb-forwarding-command)

Common MDB Forwarding Command

This command forwards raw MDB commands (including MDB CHK), with the MDB mode bit removed.

Request Packet:

Mode

Data

Request 00H

VMC Request Command

(Reset,Setup,Reader,Expansion,Vend)

Response Packet:

Mode

Data

Response 01H

Peripheral Response

Example: MIB -> Q3V 09 04 00 10 10 E0 0D

Q3V -> MIB 09 04 01 00 00 FF 0D.

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#begin-session-command)

Begin Session Command

When the application is ready for a transaction, it issues a begin session command to inform the VMC master. This marks the beginning of a transaction. Balance amount is 2 bytes; if balance does not exist, fill with 0xFF. This command follows MDB spec definition but is initiated by the app.

Request Packet:

Mode

Data

Request 00H

Begin Session (03H) + Funds Available + MDB Checksum

Response Packet:

Mode

Data

Response 01H

ACK 00H

Example: Q3V -> MIB 09 06 00 03 00 64 67 32 0d

MIB -> Q3V 09 03 01 00 ff 0d

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/mdb-communication-protocal#session-cancel-request-0x04)

Session Cancel Request(0x04)

The application can end a payment session by issuing a session cancel request command. The POS acts as the master during this command.

Request Packet:

Mode

Data

Request 00H

Cancel Session Req(04H) + Funds Available + Checksum

Response Packet:

Mode

Data

Response 01H

ACK 00H

# Java API Samples | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/java-api-samples#java-api-samples)

Java API Samples

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/java-api-samples#overview)

Overview

Explore the power of the CloudPOS Java API with these practical examples. Before diving in, ensure you have the latest CloudPOS SDK AAR file, available for download at CloudPOS SDK AAR. Replace any outdated files as necessary.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/cloudpos-sdk/java-api-samples#cloudpos-api-demos)

# PINPAD | CloudPOS SDK

*   **Input PIN specification**
    

If no input is entered, it will timeout after 1 minute, and the interval for each PIN input is 10s after the input begins

*   **\-97536(0x17d00) means operation is canceled**
    

Logs are like:

`######Hooker::HOOKER_CTRL_EVENT_Cancel`

`HAL_Pinpad : Operation canceled`

*   **Encrypt specification**
    

Plain date should be multiple of 8.

*   \-76800 means break rules about data sensitivity
    

For master key/transport key, can not inject same key with the current existed key in the slot.

For user key(session key), under the protection of a master key, the injected userkey cannot be the same as the existed userkeys.

Please notice, for every bytes of the key, if only the last bit of the byte is different, that is same too.

# Recover a Tampered Terminal | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/recover-a-tampered-terminal#overview)

Overview

This guide explains the process for recovering a Smart POS terminal that has entered a tamper status. This status can only be resolved by the terminal vendor (WizarPOS). Unauthorized attempts to recover the terminal are not permitted.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/recover-a-tampered-terminal#steps-for-recovery)

Steps for Recovery

1\. **Token Generation During Booting:** When the terminal boots, it generates a token. This token is stored in the TF card.

2\. **Sending the Token File:** You need to retrieve this token file and email it to WizarPOS for recovery. Use the following details for your email:

*   **Subject:** "Request for Device Recovery from Tamper Status"
    
*   **Recipient:** team.support@wizarpos.com (and include your WizarPOS sales contact in CC)
    
*   **Email Body:** Include your Company or Group name as registered in our Terminal Management System (TMS). Note: Without this information, we cannot process your request.
    
*   **Attachment**: Attach the token file from the TF card.
    

3\. **Choose the Tamper Reason:** Indicate the reason for tampering in your email. Options include:

*   Received the device tampered from WizarPOS
    
*   Tampered during repair
    
*   Tampered due to falling or dropping
    

4\. **Receiving the Signature File:** After we receive and approve your request, we will respond with a signature file attached (.sig file).

5\. **Final Recovery Step:**

*   Place the .sig file in the same folder as the token file on the TF card.
    
*   Reboot the terminal. Ensure that both the token and signature files are in the same folder for successful recovery.
    

circle-info

**Note:**

This process is exclusive to authorized personnel. Unauthorized attempts to recover a tampered terminal are strictly prohibited and may result in further complications.

[PreviousHardware/Repairchevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair)
[NextLearning Tampered Eventschevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/learning-tampered-events)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Overview](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/recover-a-tampered-terminal#overview)
    
*   [Steps for Recovery](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/recover-a-tampered-terminal#steps-for-recovery)

# Fingerprint Data Formats | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-data-formats#crossmatch-fingerprint-module)

Crossmatch Fingerprint Module

Supported Data Types/Formats:

*   DigitalPersona
    
*   ANSI
    
*   ISO
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-data-formats#wizarpos-fingerprint-module)

WizarPOS Fingerprint Module

Supported Data Types/Formats:

*   RawData
    
*   ANSI
    
*   ISO
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-data-formats#overview)

Overview

*   Both Crossmatch and WizarPOS fingerprint modules support a range of data types and template formats, including ANSI and ISO standards.
    
*   The Crossmatch module additionally supports the DigitalPersona format.
    
*   The WizarPOS module uniquely supports RawData format.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-data-formats#implications-for-development)

Implications for Development

*   Understanding these supported formats is essential for developers when integrating fingerprint functionality into their applications.
    
*   It ensures compatibility and efficient data handling in applications utilizing these fingerprint modules.

# Learning Tampered Events | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/learning-tampered-events#what-causes-the-terminal-to-trigger)

What Causes the Terminal to Trigger

*   **Disassembly:** Attempting to disassemble the terminal.
    
*   **Physical Damage:** Dropping or breaking the terminal.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/learning-tampered-events#consequences-of-a-triggered-terminal)

Consequences of a Triggered Terminal

When the terminal detects tampering or damage:

*   It will initiate a **tamper event**.
    
*   All payment-related keys are permanently deleted, disabling payment processing.
    
*   The terminal locks itself and displays a warning: **"Tamper detected! Please contact WizarPOS!"**
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/learning-tampered-events#recovery-process-for-a-triggered-terminal)

Recovery Process for a Triggered Terminal

1\. **Reporting the Issue:**

Contact WizarPOS sales or support. Provide detailed information about the incident and a 'token file' from the terminal.

2\. **Obtaining the Token File:**

*   Insert a TF-card into the affected terminal.
    
*   Restart the terminal. It will automatically generate a 'token file' on the TF-card.
    

3\. **Application for Recovery:**

*   Submit your 'token file' for review.
    
*   If approved, WizarPOS will provide a one-time reactivation ('re-active sig') file.
    

4\. **Reactivating the Terminal:**

*   Place the 're-active sig' file in the same directory as the 'token file' on the TF-card. (Do not delete the 'token file').
    
*   Restart the terminal.
    
*   Successful operation will allow the system to boot and function normally.
    

[PreviousRecover a Tampered Terminalchevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/recover-a-tampered-terminal)
[NextRemotely Reactivate from Tamperchevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/remotely-reactivate-from-tamper)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [What Causes the Terminal to Trigger](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/learning-tampered-events#what-causes-the-terminal-to-trigger)
    
*   [Consequences of a Triggered Terminal](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/learning-tampered-events#consequences-of-a-triggered-terminal)
    
*   [Recovery Process for a Triggered Terminal](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/learning-tampered-events#recovery-process-for-a-triggered-terminal)

# Remotely Reactivate from Tamper | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/remotely-reactivate-from-tamper#understanding-the-tampered-screen)

Understanding the Tampered Screen

*   ![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%2Fblobs%2FSLdlK4gis6vqEydfJoqx%2FTerminalRemoteActivationManual_pic1.jpg&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=529ba6e2&sv=2)
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/remotely-reactivate-from-tamper#configuring-activation-rules-in-tms)

Configuring Activation Rules in TMS

**Step-by-Step Guide:**

1.  **Log into TMS:** Access your Terminal Management System (TMS) account.
    
2.  **Setting Up Activation Mode:**
    
    *   Navigate to **'Terminals > Group**' and select your desired group.
        
    *   Click on **'Terminal Remote Activation Configure**'. This will open a configuration page.
        
    

![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%2Fblobs%2FLyLqoGWGLW71GBx7PEL0%2FTerminalRemoteActivationManual_pic2.jpg&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9b52116b&sv=2)

**Activation Modes:**

*   **Disable:** Remote activation is not possible. Only local TF card activation is allowed.
    
*   **Automatic Activation:** Terminals activate immediately upon clicking the **'ACTIVATE**' button, without requiring an activation code. This method is convenient but less secure.
    
*   **Activation Code:** Set a 6-16 character activation code. Regular updates to the code are advised for enhanced security.
    
*   **Email Activation Code:** Enter an email to receive a one-time, non-reusable activation code. This is the most secure method.
    
*   After choosing the mode, click the **'Commit**' button to finalize settings.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/remotely-reactivate-from-tamper#pos-activation-operation)

POS Activation Operation

*   Ensure the terminal is connected to the Internet.
    
*   ### 
    
    [hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/remotely-reactivate-from-tamper#click-the-activate-button-on-the-terminal)
    
    Click the **'ACTIVATE**' button on the terminal.
    
    *   **Automatic Activation:** The terminal activates immediately.
        
    *   **Activation Code/Email Activation Code:** Enter the activation code set in TMS or received via email.
        
    
*   ![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%2Fblobs%2FIRvO3wibO8ZOpnbNoauq%2FTerminalRemoteActivationManual_pic3.jpg&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b40d3d03&sv=2)
    
*   After successful activation, a **'REBOOT**' button appears.
    
*   Click **'REBOOT**' to restart the terminal, allowing it to enter the system.
    

![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%2Fblobs%2FeRDHLJFc6ACOSQdO89bm%2FTerminalRemoteActivationManual_pic4.jpg&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a70e3d95&sv=2)

[PreviousLearning Tampered Eventschevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/learning-tampered-events)
[NextTF (Micro SD) Card Suggestionchevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/hardware-repair/tf-micro-sd-card-suggestion)

# Preserve Terminal Battery Life | CloudPOS SDK

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/preserve-terminal-battery-life#preserving-terminal-batteries-during-prolonged-non-use)

Preserving Terminal Batteries During Prolonged Non-Use

To ensure the longevity of your terminal and prevent internal battery leakage, it is recommended to recharge the terminal every six months. This regular charging helps maintain the battery's health and extends the overall lifespan of the terminal.

[PreviousUnderstand Special Charging Indicatorchevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-special-charging-indicator)

Last updated 1 year ago

# TF (Micro SD) Card Suggestion | CloudPOS SDK

1.  **Capacity Range:** Choose between 4GB to 32GB. This range is ideal for ensuring efficient storage and performance in Smart POS applications.
    
2.  **Required Format**: The TF card should be formatted in the FAT32 file system. This format is compatible with the Android environment used in Smart POS systems.
    
3.  **Partitioning:** Avoid creating multiple partitions on the TF card. A single partition ensures smoother operation and compatibility with the Smart POS device.
    
4.  **Recommended Brand:** SanDisk is a preferred brand. Their TF cards have been tested for reliability and performance in Smart POS systems.
    

**Note:** When selecting a TF card for your Smart POS device, consider the above specifications to ensure optimal performance and compatibility. The recommended brand is based on industry experience and may vary depending on availability and specific device requirements.

![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3254882245-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%252Fuploads%252F0sFGp4UCq3eBGdMuCv3D%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D299c8758-577f-4b7e-ad9a-bdd607deb399&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9373e091&sv=2)

Picture 1(SanDisk)

# Understand Special Charging Indicator | CloudPOS SDK

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-special-charging-indicator#indicator-behavior)

Indicator Behavior:

When you connect the USB charger to your device, the charging indicator LED will initially flash red slowly. Following this, all four LEDs will flash simultaneously.

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-special-charging-indicator#what-this-means)

What This Means:

This specific pattern of flashing LEDs is an alert that the device's battery is excessively discharged.

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-special-charging-indicator#immediate-action-required)

Immediate Action Required:

To address this, continue charging the device using the adapter for a minimum of 5 minutes. This extended charging period is necessary to recover the battery from its overly discharged state.

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-special-charging-indicator#expected-outcome)

Expected Outcome:

After charging for the recommended duration, your battery should return to a normal state, indicated by the standard charging LED behavior.

Note: Regularly allowing your battery to become overly discharged can affect its overall lifespan and performance. It is advisable to charge your device before the battery level becomes too low.

[PreviousBattery/Powerchevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power)
[NextPreserve Terminal Battery Lifechevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/preserve-terminal-battery-life)

# Install CA Certificates | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/install-ca-certificates#for-android-12)

For Android 12:

1.  Navigate to Settings > Security > Encryption & credentials.
    
2.  Select Install a certificate > CA certificate.
    
3.  Follow the on-screen instructions to complete the installation.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/install-ca-certificates#for-other-android-versions)

For Other Android Versions:

1.  Save the CA certificate to a TF card.
    
2.  Insert the TF card into the terminal.
    
3.  On the terminal, go to Settings > Security > Install from SD card.
    
4.  Select the CA certificate from the TF card.
    
5.  When prompted, enter a name for the certificate.
    
6.  Set a lock screen PIN if required.
    
7.  A confirmation message will display upon successful installation of the CA certificate.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/install-ca-certificates#important-notes)

Important Notes:

*   Third-party apps cannot install a CA certificate on the terminal programmatically without UI interaction for security reasons. Only system APKs have this capability.
    
*   It is crucial to follow these steps to ensure the secure and correct installation of CA certificates.
    

[PreviousRenew App Certificatechevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/renew-app-certificate)
[NextClear Terminal Certificateschevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/clear-terminal-certificates)

# Understand Terminal Battery Performance | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-terminal-battery-performance#time-for-full-discharge-during-use)

Time for Full Discharge (During Use)

The duration for a complete discharge varies depending on how the terminal is used. Below are the estimated discharge times under normal usage conditions, which include constant light mode, default brightness, and 4G usage, starting from a full battery (100%) to shutdown:

*   Q1V2: Approximately 6 hours
    
*   Q2: Approximately 6.5 hours
    
*   Q3: Approximately 7.5 hours
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-terminal-battery-performance#time-for-full-charge-0-100)

Time for Full Charge (0-100%)

When charging the terminal with a 5V2A power supply in constant light mode, the time taken to charge the battery from 0% to 100% is as follows:

*   Q1V2: Approximately 2.5 hours
    
*   Q2: Approximately 2.6 hours
    
*   Q3: Approximately 4 hours
    

Important Note: The actual time for discharge and charge may vary depending on the specific model of the terminal and the operating conditions. Battery performance can be influenced by factors such as the age of the battery, environmental conditions, and specific usage patterns.

[PreviousUnderstand Q2 Low-voltage Shutdownchevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-q2-low-voltage-shutdown)
[NextUnderstand Counter Modechevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-counter-mode)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Time for Full Discharge (During Use)](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-terminal-battery-performance#time-for-full-discharge-during-use)
    
*   [Time for Full Charge (0-100%)](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-terminal-battery-performance#time-for-full-charge-0-100)

# Understand Certificate Visibility | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/understand-certificate-visibility#overview)

Overview

Users may encounter situations where a custom user certificate, imported through the device settings, does not appear on Q2 terminals.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/understand-certificate-visibility#key-steps-for-importing-certificates)

Key Steps for Importing Certificates

1.  Navigate to Trusted Certificates:
    
    *   Go to Settings > Security > Encryption > Trusted Certificates > Users.
        
    
2.  Import the Certificate:
    
    *   Proceed with importing the desired user certificate.
        
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/understand-certificate-visibility#important-note)

Important Note

Certificate Attribute Requirement:

*   For a certificate to be listed on a Q2 terminal, it must have the 'isCA' flag set to true.
    
*   If this flag is not set to true, the certificate will not be visible or listed on the terminal.
    

This section clarifies the specific attribute requirement for certificates to be recognized and listed on Q2 terminals, aiding users in troubleshooting issues related to certificate visibility.

# Fingerprint DPI Specifications | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-dpi-specifications#crossmatch-fingerprint-module)

Crossmatch Fingerprint Module

*   Array Size: 256 x 360 pixels.
    
*   Image Resolution: 508 DPI (dots per inch).
    
*   Gray Scale: 8-bit (256 levels).
    
*   Imaging Area: 18.00 mm x 12.80 mm.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-dpi-specifications#wizarpos-fingerprint-module)

WizarPOS Fingerprint Module

*   Array Size: 360 x 256 pixels.
    
*   Image Resolution: 508 DPI (dots per inch).
    
*   Gray Scale: 8-bit.
    
*   Active Sensing Area: 18.0 mm x 12.8 mm.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-dpi-specifications#key-points)

Key Points

*   Both Crossmatch and WizarPOS fingerprint modules offer a high image resolution of 508 DPI, ensuring detailed fingerprint capture.
    
*   The array size and gray scale specifications are critical for developers to understand the image quality and the level of detail that can be captured by these modules.
    

[PreviousFingerprint Module Usage Guidechevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-module-usage-guide)
[NextFingerprint Data Formatschevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-data-formats)

Last updated 1 year ago

# NFC Buffer Size Understanding | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/nfc-buffer-size-understanding#overview)

Overview

This section details the buffer size for Near Field Communication (NFC) readers used in POS systems.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/nfc-buffer-size-understanding#buffer-size-details)

Buffer Size Details

*   Fixed Buffer Size:
    
    *   The buffer size of the NFC reader is set at 256 bytes.
        
    
*   Compliance and Limitations:
    
    *   This buffer size complies with EMV (Europay, Mastercard, and Visa) standards.
        
    *   It is important to note that this buffer size cannot be modified or adjusted.
        
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/nfc-buffer-size-understanding#implications)

Implications

*   The fixed buffer size of 256 bytes is designed to ensure reliable and standardized transaction processing in line with EMV requirements.
    
*   Users and developers should account for this limitation in their application design and usage of NFC readers.
    

[PreviousContactless Card Distancechevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/contactless-card-distance)
[NextUse Contactless CPU Cardchevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/use-contactless-cpu-card)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Overview](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/nfc-buffer-size-understanding#overview)
    
*   [Buffer Size Details](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/nfc-buffer-size-understanding#buffer-size-details)
    
*   [Implications](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/nfc-buffer-size-understanding#implications)

# Contactless Card Distance | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/contactless-card-distance#overview)

Overview

This section outlines the effective reading distances for contactless cards when used with different models of Smart POS terminals.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/contactless-card-distance#reading-distance-specifications)

Reading Distance Specifications

*   Model Q1:
    
    *   Effective reading distance: 0 to 2 cm.
        
    
*   Model Q2:
    
    *   Effective reading distance: 0 to 4 cm.
        
    
*   Model Q3:
    
    *   Effective reading distance: 0 to 4 cm.
        
    

circle-info

**Note:**

*   These distances represent the maximum range at which the POS terminal can successfully read a contactless card.
    
*   Users should ensure that the card is within this range for optimal functionality and transaction processing.

# Clear Terminal Certificates | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/clear-terminal-certificates#prerequisites)

Prerequisites

*   Ensure Administrator Login is completed. For engineer mode terminals, login is default.
    
*   Have a TF-card ready for use.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/clear-terminal-certificates#steps-to-generate-and-verify-token)

Steps to Generate and Verify Token

1.  Insert the TF-card into the Terminal:
    
    *   Place the TF-card in the designated slot on the terminal.
        
    
2.  Navigate to Certificate Management:
    
    *   Go to Settings > About POS > POS Configuration > Certificate Management.
        
    
3.  Generate Token:
    
    *   Choose Clear Certificates.
        
    *   Select the Generate token radio button.
        
    *   Click the Confirm button. This action generates a token file in the root path of the TF-card.
        
    *   A notification will appear in the notification bar upon completion.
        
    
4.  Send Token File to WizarPOS:
    
    *   Transfer the token file from the TF-card to your computer.
        
    *   Email the token file to WizarPOS for signing.
        
    *   WizarPOS will return a signed '.sig' file.
        
    
5.  Verify Token:
    
    *   Place the '.sig' file on the TF-card, in the same location as the token file.
        
    *   Reinsert the TF-card into the terminal.
        
    *   Return to 'Certificate Management' and select 'Clear Certificates'.
        
    *   Choose the 'Verify token' radio button and click 'Confirm'.
        
    *   A notification will appear in the notification bar upon successful verification.
        
    
6.  Restart and Confirm Clearance:
    
    *   Restart the terminal.
        
    *   Navigate to Settings > About POS > POS Configuration > Certificate Management > Certificate List.
        
    *   Verify that all certificates have been cleared.
        
    

circle-info

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/clear-terminal-certificates#important-notes)

Important Notes

*   These steps must be performed with administrative privileges.
    
*   Ensure that the TF-card is correctly inserted and recognized by the terminal before proceeding with each step.
    

[PreviousInstall CA Certificateschevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/install-ca-certificates)
[NextUnderstand Certificate Visibilitychevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/understand-certificate-visibility)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Prerequisites](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/clear-terminal-certificates#prerequisites)
    
*   [Steps to Generate and Verify Token](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/clear-terminal-certificates#steps-to-generate-and-verify-token)

# Understand Q2 Low-voltage Shutdown | CloudPOS SDK

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-q2-low-voltage-shutdown#understanding-the-q2-terminals-auto-shutdown-due-to-low-battery-voltage)

Understanding the Q2 Terminal's Auto-Shutdown Due to Low Battery Voltage

The Q2 terminal is designed to automatically shut down when its battery level reaches 3%. This feature is implemented to preserve the integrity of the device and prevent damage caused by excessively low battery levels.

# Understand PSAM Card Exceptions | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/understand-psam-card-exceptions#overview)

Overview

This section details the common exceptions encountered when using the SmartCardReaderDevice.open method in Q2/Q3 series devices for PSAM cards.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/understand-psam-card-exceptions#common-exception-scenarios)

Common Exception Scenarios

1.  No Physical SAM Card Inserted:
    
    *   When attempting to open the PSAM card reader without a physical SAM card inserted, the system will throw an exception.
        
    *   Exception Details: 'Code:-6 com.cloudpos.DeviceException: Operation error! Error code = -1, Error message = Operation not permitted'.
        
    
2.  Device Restart Required After PSAM Card Insertion:
    
    *   Inserting a PSAM card into the terminal does not support hot plugging. Therefore, the device needs to be restarted after insertion.
        
    *   If the device is not restarted, the PSAM card will not be recognized, leading to an exception.
        
    *   Same exception details as above will apply in this scenario.
        
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/understand-psam-card-exceptions#important-notes)

Important Notes

*   It is essential to ensure that a PSAM card is physically present in the reader before attempting to use the SmartCardReaderDevice.open method.
    
*   Always restart the device after inserting a PSAM card to ensure proper recognition and functionality.
    

[PreviousUse Mifare Cardchevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/use-mifare-card)
[NextOptimal Tap Positioning Guidechevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/optimal-tap-positioning-guide)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Overview](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/understand-psam-card-exceptions#overview)
    
*   [Common Exception Scenarios](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/understand-psam-card-exceptions#common-exception-scenarios)
    
*   [Important Notes](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/understand-psam-card-exceptions#important-notes)

# Renew App Certificate | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/renew-app-certificate#generating-and-sending-csr-certificate-signing-request)

Generating and Sending CSR (Certificate Signing Request)

*   **Choose the original keystore which use to sign APK currently. Because this step is to renew certificate in the keystore, not create a new certificate. If create new keystore, APK can not update again.**
    
*   Export CSR:
    
    *   Follow the standard procedure to generate a CSR using keytool.
        
    

Copy

     keytool -certreq -keystore demo.jks -alias androiddebugkey > demo.csr
     
     Note: 
       demo.jks is the keystore, it can be the keytore path+name.
       androiddebugkey is the alias of the private key. It should be the real alias of the private key which using to sign APK in your keystore.
       demo.csr can be any name, suffix is .csr.

*   Submit CSR to WizarPOS:
    
    *   Email the CSR with the following details:
        
        *   Sales Person: Name of your WizarPOS contact.
            
        *   Company Name: Your company's name.
            
        *   Attachment: Include the CSR file.
            
        *   Email body: Renew app ceritificate.
            
        
    *   Send to: WizarPOS sales staff (add first), support@wizarpos.com, team.support@wizarpos.com.
        
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/renew-app-certificate#import-the-certificate-chain)

Import the Certificate Chain

Save the WizarPOS reply (in \*.crt or \*.pem format) , then use keytool to import the certificate to the keystore again.

*   Import the Certificate Chain:
    
    *   Use the appropriate tool to import the certificate chain file into your keystore.
        
    *   During the import process, when prompted to trust the certificate, input "Y" or the equivalent affirmative option in your language.
        
    

[PreviousApply App Certificateschevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/apply-app-certificates)
[NextInstall CA Certificateschevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/install-ca-certificates)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Generating and Sending CSR (Certificate Signing Request)](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/renew-app-certificate#generating-and-sending-csr-certificate-signing-request)
    
*   [Import the Certificate Chain](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/certificate/renew-app-certificate#import-the-certificate-chain)
    

Copy

     keytool -importcert -keystore demo.jks -file file-name-of-CSR-reply -alias androiddebugkey
     
     Note: 
       demo.jks is the keystore, it should be same keystore with the keystore when export CSR.
       androiddebugkey is the alias of the private key. It should be the real alias of the private key which using to sign APK in your keystore.

# Use Contactless CPU Card | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/use-contactless-cpu-card#overview)

Overview

This section provides a step-by-step guide on using the Java API for interacting with contactless CPU cards.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/use-contactless-cpu-card#steps-for-java-api-usage)

Steps for Java API Usage

*   Get RFCardReaderDevice:
    

Retrieve the instance of the RFCardReaderDevice to initiate communication with the contactless card reader.

Copy

      device = (RFCardReaderDevice) POSTerminal.getInstance(mContext).getDevice(POSTerminal.DEVICE_NAME_RF_CARD_READER);

*   Open Device:
    

Execute the command to open the card reader device. This step establishes a connection between the Java application and the card reader.

Copy

      device.open();

*   Search for Card:
    

Initiate a search for the contactless CPU card. This involves scanning for available cards within the reader's range.

Copy

      OperationListener listener = new OperationListener() {
        @Override
        public void handleResult(OperationResult arg0) {
          if (arg0.getResultCode() == OperationResult.SUCCESS) {
            sendSuccessLog2(mContext.getString(R.string.find_card_succeed));
            rfCard = ((RFCardReaderOperationResult) arg0).getCard();
          } else {
            sendFailedLog2(mContext.getString(R.string.find_card_failed));
          }
        }
      };
      device.listenForCardPresent(listener, TimeConstants.FOREVER); The result will be returned in the callback listener.

*   Communicate with Card:
    

Once the card is detected, establish communication. This step may involve reading from or writing to the card, depending on the application's requirements.

*   Close Device:
    

After the communication with the card is complete, close the device to end the session. This step is crucial for maintaining device security and integrity.

circle-info

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/use-contactless-cpu-card#important-notes)

Important Notes

*   Each step should be performed in sequence to ensure successful communication with the contactless CPU card.
    
*   Handle exceptions and errors appropriately to maintain the stability of your application.

        CPUCard cpucard = ((CPUCard) rfCard);

# Use Mifare Card | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/use-mifare-card#overview)

Overview

This section provides a step-by-step guide on using Java API for operations involving contactless Mifare cards.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/use-mifare-card#steps-for-java-api-usage)

Steps for Java API Usage

*   Get RFCardReaderDevice:
    

Initiate the process by retrieving an instance of the RFCardReaderDevice. This is crucial for establishing communication with the Mifare card reader.

Copy

      device = (RFCardReaderDevice) POSTerminal.getInstance(mContext).getDevice(POSTerminal.DEVICE_NAME_RF_CARD_READER);

*   Open Device:
    

Execute the command to open the card reader device. This step establishes a connection between your Java application and the card reader

Copy

      device.open();

*   Search for Card:
    

Start a search operation to detect the contactless Mifare card within the reader's range.

Copy

      OperationListener listener = new OperationListener() {
        @Override
        public void handleResult(OperationResult arg0) {
          if (arg0.getResultCode() == OperationResult.SUCCESS) {
            sendSuccessLog2(mContext.getString(R.string.find_card_succeed));
            rfCard = ((RFCardReaderOperationResult) arg0).getCard();
          } else {
            sendFailedLog2(mContext.getString(R.string.find_card_failed));
          }
        }
      };
      device.listenForCardPresent(listener, TimeConstants.FOREVER); The result will be returned in the callback listener.

*   Read from Card:
    

Once the card is detected, execute read operations as required. This may involve accessing data stored on the card.

*   Write to Card:
    

Perform write operations to modify or add data to the Mifare card, as per your application’s needs.

*   Close Device:
    

After completing the read/write operations, close the device to end the communication session. This is important for maintaining the security and integrity of both the card and the reader.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/use-mifare-card#important-notes)

Important Notes

*   Follow the steps sequentially to ensure successful interaction with contactless Mifare cards.
    
*   Handle exceptions and errors appropriately for smooth and secure application functionality.

*   [Important Notes](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/use-mifare-card#important-notes)

      // demo for sector 1, block 2
      int sectorIndex=1; 
      int blockIndex =2;
      if (rfCard instanceof MifareCard) {
         byte[] key = new byte[]{
                    (byte) 0xFF, (byte) 0xFF, (byte) 0xFF, (byte) 0xFF, (byte) 0xFF,
                    (byte) 0xFF
            };

                   byte[] result = card.readBlock(sectorIndex, blockIndex);

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/usb-serial-port/install-terminal-usb-drivers#frequently-asked-questions-faq)

Frequently Asked Questions (FAQ):

**Issue: Fastboot Not Detecting Device in Windows 10**

*   **Problem Description:**
    
*   Sometimes, in Windows 10, Fastboot may fail to detect the device. This issue typically indicates that the USB driver for Fastboot needs to be reinstalled.
    

1.  Download the Fastboot USB driver [herearrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/usbdriver_w10_fastboot.zip)
    .
    
2.  Unzip the downloaded file.
    
3.  Right-click on the file named 'android\_winusb.inf'.
    
4.  Select 'Install' from the context menu.
    
5.  Once the installation is complete, Fastboot should function correctly.
    

For additional support or information, please refer to our comprehensive support documentation or contact our technical helpdesk.

# Understanding Image Print Gaps | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/understanding-image-print-gaps#issue-description)

Issue Description:

When printing images continuously on a receipt, a small blank line may appear between the first and second image.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/understanding-image-print-gaps#cause)

Cause:

*   **Default Driver Configuration:** The printer driver is configured to process images in segments of 24-dot lines.
    
*   **Image Height Alignment:** If the height of the first image is not an exact multiple of 24 dots, the driver will align the image to the nearest 24-dot line. This alignment results in a blank line, the width of which is determined by the remainder of the height divided by 24.
    

[PreviousJava API Printer Operationschevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/java-api-printer-operations)
[NextPrint with JavaScriptchevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/print-with-javascript)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Issue Description:](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/understanding-image-print-gaps#issue-description)
    
*   [Cause:](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/understanding-image-print-gaps#cause)

# Understand Counter Mode | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-counter-mode#why-counter-mode-is-necessary)

Why Counter Mode is Necessary:

*   The Q3/Q2Premium terminal utilizes a soft battery.
    
*   Continuous charging, especially when the battery is already fully charged, can lead to battery bulging.
    
*   To mitigate this risk, software adjustments are made to the charging mechanism.
    
*   Counter Mode is essential when the charger is constantly connected to the terminal.
    
*   In Counter Mode, the battery recharges at 15% (rather than the usual 95%) to avoid long-term full charge. The recharge capacity can be set by parameter file.
    
*   In Counter Mode, charging terminates at 88% capacity, whereas in non-counter mode, charging continues until it reaches 100%. The terminate capacity can not be changed.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-counter-mode#how-to-activate-counter-mode)

How to Activate Counter Mode:

There is the auto-counter mode algorithm in the Q3 terminal.

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-counter-mode#manual-activation-in-terminal-settings)

Manual Activation in Terminal Settings:

*   Navigate to Settings > Administrator Login.
    
*   Go to Setting > Battery.
    
*   Toggle Counter Mode on or off as needed.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-counter-mode#activation-via-apk-installation)

Activation via APK Installation:

*   Install the specific APK to automatically set the terminal to Counter Mode.
    
*   This APK disables the auto-counter mode algorithm, allowing for unconditional Counter Mode activation.
    
*   No app icon is displayed on the launcher desktop.
    
*   Two versions of the APK are available: one to turn on Counter Mode, and another to turn it off (both updated as of 8/28/2023).
    
    *   [APK to turn on Counter Mode(updated 8/28/2023)arrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/ChargeCounter-release-v3.0.2_counter_on-r20230823172106-q1_platform.apk)
        
    *   [APK to turn off Counter Mode(updated 8/28/2023)arrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/ChargeCounter-release-v3.0.2_counter_off-r20230823164102-q1_platform.apk)
        
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-counter-mode#activation-via-tms-terminal-management-system)

Activation via TMS (Terminal Management System):

*   Add a new parameter file in WizarView. Follow steps in the WizarView application to upload and commit the parameter file.
    
    *   Access Application Settings:
        
        *   Navigate to the 'Applications' section, and then select 'Application' from the submenu.
            
        
    *   Add New Parameter File:
        
        *   Click the '+' icon located at the bottom left of the toolbox. This will open an edit window.
            
        *   In the edit window, fill in the required fields, including the name of the parameter file.
            
        *   Ensure to select 'param' as the type.
            
        *   Enter the package name, which should be 'com.wizarpos.system.settings', and then the name of your parameter file.
            
        *   After entering all the details, click the 'Commit' button to save this entry.
            
        
    *   Locate the New Parameter File:
        
        *   Now, click the 'Search' button in the 'Applications > Application' page.
            
        *   From the displayed list, select the parameter file you just added.
            
        
    *   Configure the Parameter File:
        
        *   Click the configuration (config) icon located at the right bottom of the toolbox.
            
        *   In the popup window, click the 'Upload' button.
            
        
    *   Upload the Parameter File:
        
        *   Choose the appropriate parameter file from your device.
            
        *   Once selected, click the 'Commit' button to upload the file to the system.
            
        
    
*   This allows the configuration of the terminal remotely via file push, similar to application updates.
    

![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3254882245-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%252Fuploads%252FWKC9spBwlZ4N0KEc8xcX%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D448b3ec3-3f6b-4082-be18-25026b3f416f&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bdcac9b9&sv=2)

![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3254882245-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%252Fuploads%252FQcAC8akD1jBZx3SBSLZz%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D24406a2d-9f7f-49b8-b97c-aef3f635ef78&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ff9ab957&sv=2)

*   Parameter files are available to turn on or off Counter Mode.
    
    *   [Sample paramter file to turn on Counter Modearrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/counter_true.json)
        
    *   [Sample parameter file to turn off Counter Modearrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/counter_false.json)
        
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/battery-power/understand-counter-mode#activation-through-api-application-programming-interface)

Activation through API (Application Programming Interface):

*   Add the required permission, '<uses-permission android:name="android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_SET\_BATTERY\_COUNTER\_MODE" />' in 'AndroidManifest.xml'.
    
*   Utilize the [AIDL filearrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/ISystemExtApi.aidl)
     in the package 'com.wizarpos.wizarviewagentassistant.aidl'.
    
*   A code sample can be provided for this purpose.
    

By using Counter Mode in the appropriate situations, the lifespan and health of the terminal's battery can be significantly enhanced.

    public void systemExtApiService_setBatteryCounterMode(Context context, boolean enable) {
        ServiceConnection systemExtConn = new ServiceConnection() {
            @Override
            public void onServiceConnected(ComponentName name, IBinder service) {
                ISystemExtApi systemExtApiService = ISystemExtApi.Stub.asInterface(service);
                Logger.debug("startAgentService = " + systemExtApiService);
                try {
                    systemExtApiService.setBatteryCounterMode(enable);
                } catch (RemoteException e) {
                    e.printStackTrace();
                }
            }
    
            @Override
            public void onServiceDisconnected(ComponentName name) {
            }
        };
        ComponentName comp = new ComponentName("com.wizarpos.wizarviewagentassistant","com.wizarpos.wizarviewagentassistant.SystemExtApiService");
        Intent intent = new Intent();
        intent.setComponent(comp);
        context.bindService(intent, systemExtConn, Context.BIND_AUTO_CREATE);
        context.startService(intent);
    }

# Fingerprint Module Usage Guide | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-module-usage-guide#adding-required-permissions)

Adding Required Permissions

Manifest File Configuration:

*   Add the following permission to your application's manifest file:'<uses-permission android:name="android.permission.CLOUDPOS\_FINGERPRINT" />'
    
*   Ensure that permissions are correctly set in the manifest file to avoid operational issues with the fingerprint module.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-module-usage-guide#using-crossmatch-fingerprint-module)

Using Crossmatch Fingerprint Module

SDK and Documentation:

*   To develop applications compatible with the Crossmatch fingerprint module, download the necessary SDK and documentation.
    
*   Basic SDK (TCS1FingerPrintSDK):
    
    *   Use this SDK for basic operations like fingerprint input and image acquisition.
        
    
*   Advanced SDK (U.are.U SDK):
    
    *   Utilize this SDK for more complex functions like fingerprint comparison or compression.
        
    *   Note: The U.are.U SDK should not be used for fingerprint input. Specifically, the 'Reader' class from this SDK is not applicable for input purposes in your application.
        
    *   It is crucial to integrate the appropriate SDK based on your application’s requirements.
        
    

Files to download

Description

[TCS1FingerPrintSDKarrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/device/TCS1FingerPrintSDK_demo&javadoc_20231103.zip)

Crossmatch fingerprint basic demo and javadoc API

Crossmatch fingerprint UareU demo and javadoc API

 here.

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/fingerprint/fingerprint-module-usage-guide#api-document)

API document

Please find _com.cloudpos.fingerprint_ from [java api docarrow-up-right](http://sdkwiki.wizarpos.com/wizarposapi/)
.

*   Compare ISO 2005 template, please use method compare, compareByFormat and identify;
    
*   Compare ANSI 378 template, please use method compareByFormat(byte\[\] arryBuffer1, int format1, byte\[\] arryBuffer2, int format2);
    
*   Convert between ISO 2005 and ANSI 378 template format, please use convertFormat(byte\[\] dataBuffer, int srcFormat, int outFormat).

        String prop = getProperty("wp.fingerprint.model","");
            if (prop.equalsIgnoreCase("none")) {
                showNormalDialog("tips", "No fingerprint module.");
            } else if (prop.equalsIgnoreCase("tuzhengbig")) {
               //WizarPOS FP
            } else if (prop.equalsIgnoreCase("crossmatch")) {
               //Crossmatch FP
            }    
        public static String getProperty(String key, String defaultValue) {
            String value = defaultValue;
            try {
                Class<?> c = Class.forName("android.os.SystemProperties");
                Method get = c.getMethod("get", String.class, String.class);
                value = (String)(get.invoke(c, key, defaultValue ));
            } catch (Exception e) {
                e.printStackTrace();
            }finally {
                return value;
            }
        }

# Linux Serial Driver Installation | CloudPOS SDK

This guide provides step-by-step instructions for downloading and installing the USB driver for your production terminal on a Linux system.

**Download and Preparation:**

*   Download the USB Driver:
    
    *   Download the USB driver zip package from the provided link: [USB Driver Zip Packagearrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/usbserialdriverinlinux.zip)
        .
        
    
*   Unzip the Package:
    
    *   After downloading, unzip the package to a preferred location on your system.
        
    

**Installation Steps:**

1.  **Compile the Driver:**
    
    *   Open your terminal.
        
    *   Navigate to the directory where you unzipped the package.
        
    *   Run the command: **'make**'
        
    
2.  **Load the usbserial Module:**
    
    *   Execute the command: **'sudo modprobe usbserial**'
        
    
3.  **Insert the Driver Module:**
    
    *   Insert the driver module by running: **'sudo insmod ./qcgeneric.ko**'
        
    
4.  **Verify the Installation:**
    
    *   Check if the driver is successfully installed and recognized by your system with the command: **'ll /dev/ttyUSB\***'
        
    *   This command lists all the USB serial devices connected to your system.
        
    

If you encounter any issues during the installation process, please refer to our FAQ section or contact our technical support team for assistance.

# Optimal Tap Positioning Guide | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/optimal-tap-positioning-guide#overview)

Overview

This section provides guidelines on the best position for tapping a card on Q3-series terminals, specifically models like Q3F, which feature front contactless readers

![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3254882245-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%252Fuploads%252FORmUcODVEN7v0GZwEU7M%252Fbestrfposition.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8ea6f057-f03d-49fd-89c1-afe8a1696a85&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4b4b77e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/optimal-tap-positioning-guide#app-design-considerations)

App Design Considerations

Developer's Role:

*   In applications designed for these terminals, developers should include prompts or guides indicating the optimal card tap position.
    
*   This guidance is crucial to ensure users are aware of the area with the strongest antenna signal for reliable card reading
    

![](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3254882245-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FTv6FkzHXX8QyxZpeenq6%252Fuploads%252FQpPzRyqDmxpXJZwy12Zu%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3321aebc-3e82-4b33-a022-62b81ac85508&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=41d60423&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/optimal-tap-positioning-guide#guidance-for-optimal-tap-position)

Guidance for Optimal Tap Position

*   The exact position for optimal card tapping should align with the area of highest antenna intensity in the terminal.
    
*   Details on this position may vary based on the specific terminal model and should be confirmed with the hardware specifications.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/card/optimal-tap-positioning-guide#important-notes)

Important Notes

*   Ensuring users tap their card at the correct spot is essential for efficient and error-free transactions.
    
*   Developers should prioritize this feature in their app designs for enhanced user experience and transaction success rates.

# Verify Printer Paper Status | CloudPOS SDK

*   **Purpose of queryStatus():**
    

This method is used to ascertain the paper status in the printer. It is especially useful for checking if paper is available before initiating a print job. In cases of printing large receipts, it may be advisable to check the paper status after printing as well.

*   When print receipt, sometime app want to know whether the receipt has finished printing, it can call this method to check too, because the printer commands are executed sequentially.
    

Copy

      device = (PrinterDevice) POSTerminal.getInstance(mContext).getDevice(POSTerminal.DEVICE_NAME_PRINTER);
      int result = device.queryStatus();
      device.close();

*   **Understanding the Result Codes:**
    
    *   **Result < 0:** Indicates an error. The specific negative value corresponds to a particular error code.
        
    *   **Result = 0:** Signifies that the printer is out of paper.
        
    *   **Result = 1:** Confirms that the printer has paper available for printing.
        
    

[PreviousPrint with JavaScriptchevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/print-with-javascript)
[NextUSB/Serial Portchevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/usb-serial-port)

# Retrieve Terminal IMEI Number | CloudPOS SDK

This guide outlines the process for obtaining the IMEI (International Mobile Equipment Identity) number of your terminal using a specific code snippet.

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/retrieve-terminal-imei-number#code-snippet-for-imei-retrieval)

Code Snippet for IMEI Retrieval

Below is the code snippet necessary for retrieving the IMEI number:

Copy

      TelephonyManager telephonyManager =
                    (TelephonyManager) context.getSystemService(Context.TELEPHONY_SERVICE);
      String imei = telephonyManager.getImei(slot index);

#### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/retrieve-terminal-imei-number#important-note-for-q2-devices-with-android-12)

Important Note for Q2 Devices with Android 12

When using this method on Q2 devices that operate on Android 12, it is important to note that the targetSDK version should be 28 or lower. This requirement is specific to Q2 devices with Android 12 and may not apply to other models or operating system versions.

# Print Images | CloudPOS SDK

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/print-images#preparing-the-image)

Preparing the Image

**Location:** Place the image in the **'assets**' folder of your application project.

**Image Specifications:**

*   **Width:** The width of the image should be 384 dots or less.
    
*   **Height:** The height should be a multiple of 24 dots. If the height is not a multiple of 24, the excess will result in blank printing at the bottom of the image.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/print-images#printing-the-image)

Printing the Image

**Using the Print Image API:** To print the image, call the print image API provided in the Java API. The necessary code snippet for this process is as follows:

Copy

        public void printBitmap(Map<String, Object> param, ActionCallback callback) {
            Bitmap bitmap =null;
            try {
                bitmap = BitmapFactory.decodeStream(mContext.getResources().getAssets()
                        .open("photo.bmp"));
            } catch (IOException e1) {
                // TODO Auto-generated catch block
                e1.printStackTrace();
            }
            try {
                device.printBitmap(bitmap);
                sendSuccessLog(mContext.getString(R.string.operation_succeed));
            } catch (DeviceException e) {
                e.printStackTrace();
                sendFailedLog(mContext.getString(R.string.operation_failed));
            }
        }

[NextPrint QR Codeschevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/printer/print-qr-codes)

Last updated 1 year ago

# Check eSIM Status | CloudPOS SDK

To check the status of an embedded SIM (e-SIM) on your WizarPOS terminal, follow these steps:

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/check-esim-status#pre-check-requirements)

Pre-Check Requirements

Before you can check the e-SIM status, ensure you have the following information:

*   Serial Number: The unique serial number of your WizarPOS terminal.
    
*   IMEI: The International Mobile Equipment Identity number of the terminal.
    
*   Data Plan Details: Information about the data plan associated with the e-SIM, including the monthly data allowance and duration of the plan.
    
*   Usage Location: The geographical location where the terminal will be used.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/check-esim-status#steps-to-check-e-sim-status)

Steps to Check e-SIM Status

1.  Access Settings: On your WizarPOS terminal, go to 'Settings'.
    
2.  Navigate to Terminal Information: Select 'About POS'.
    
3.  Open POS Configuration: Choose 'POS Configuration'.
    
4.  View Soft SIM Settings: Click on 'Soft SIM Settings' to view the status and details of your e-SIM.
    

This process will provide you with the necessary information regarding the e-SIM's activation status, data plan, and other relevant details.

[PreviousTroubleshoot Network Search Errorchevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/troubleshoot-network-search-error)
[NextEthernet Connectivity Usagechevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/ethernet-connectivity-usage)

Last updated 1 year ago

# Disable POS Hotspot | CloudPOS SDK

This guide provides three methods to disable the portable hotspot feature on your smart POS terminal: through the device's settings menu and using a dedicated application.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/disable-pos-hotspot#method-1-disabling-via-settings-menu)

Method 1: Disabling via Settings Menu

*   Access Settings: Tap on the 'Settings' icon on your terminal.
    
*   Navigate to Hotspot Settings: Follow this path: More -> Tethering & Portable Hotspot.
    
*   Turn Off the Hotspot: Select 'Portable WLAN Hotspot' and toggle it off.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/disable-pos-hotspot#method-2-disabling-via-application)

Method 2: Disabling via Application

Here is a [demoarrow-up-right](https://github.com/SmartPOSSamples/CloseHotspot)
 of disabling the portable hotspot on your smart POS terminal using a specific application.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/disable-pos-hotspot#method-3-disabling-via-wizarview)

Method 3: Disabling via Wizarview

*   Select Terminal: Go to 'Terminals' > 'Terminal'.
    
*   Choose the Desired Terminal: Identify and select the terminal you wish to configure.
    
*   Configure System Parameters: Click on the 'Config System Parameter' icon.
    
*   Access System Settings: In the popup, navigate to the 'System' tab.
    
*   Disable Hotspot: In the 'WIFI HotSpot' dropdown list, select 'Disabled'.
    
*   Commit Changes: Click 'Commit' to apply the new settings.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/disable-pos-hotspot#important-notes)

Important Notes:

*   Firmware Dependency: This feature is firmware-dependent. Disabling the hotspot through TMS will remove the 'Tethering & Portable Hotspot' menu from the terminal.
    
*   Firmware Version Requirements:
    
    *   Q2/K2/QD4/M2 models require firmware version 3962 or higher.
        
    *   Q1v2 model requires firmware version 0481 or higher.
        
    *   Q2A7 model requires firmware version 0240 or higher.
        
    

[PreviousSIM/Ethenet/WIFIchevron-left](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi)
[NextRetrieve Terminal IMEI Numberchevron-right](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/retrieve-terminal-imei-number)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Method 1: Disabling via Settings Menu](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/disable-pos-hotspot#method-1-disabling-via-settings-menu)
    
*   [Method 2: Disabling via Application](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/disable-pos-hotspot#method-2-disabling-via-application)

# Ethernet Connectivity Usage | CloudPOS SDK

This guide provides instructions on how to enable Ethernet connectivity for Q1 and Q2 WizarPOS terminals.

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/ethernet-connectivity-usage#ethernet-support-for-q1-terminal)

Ethernet Support for Q1 Terminal

1.  Connecting the Ethernet Module:
    
    *   Connect the Ethernet module to the Q1 terminal using an OTG-USB cable.
        
    
2.  Enabling Ethernet in Settings:
    
    *   Navigate to 'Settings' > 'Ethernet' to enable the Ethernet connection.
        
    *   Note for Older Firmware: If the 'Ethernet' menu is not available in your firmware version, you will need to obtain and install the [Ethernet enable control APKarrow-up-right](https://ftp.wizarpos.com/advanceSDK/EthernetCtrl_signed_DailyBuild.apk)
        . Once installed, run the APK and enable the Ethernet connection.
        
    

### 

[hashtag](https://smartpossdk.gitbook.io/cloudpossdk/faq/sim-ethenet-wifi/ethernet-connectivity-usage#ethernet-support-for-q2-terminal)

Ethernet Support for Q2 Terminal

1.  Acquiring the Ethernet Module:
    
    *   To obtain an Ethernet module for the Q2 terminal, contact WizarPOS supporter via email at team.support@wizarpos.com.
        
    
2.  Enabling Ethernet in Settings:
    
    *   Once the Ethernet module is connected, go to 'Settings' > 'Ethernet' to enable Ethernet connectivity.
